For ages the vile Doom Knights have sought to gather the remaining Thunderstones to fulfill a prophecy of corruption over the lands. Now the first Thunderstone has been discovered in the Dungeons of Grimhold and the Doom Knights have sent their minions to claim the relic. The Villagers of Barrowsdale gather brave souls to face the dungeon and keep the Thunderstone out of the hands of the Doom Knights.
\13\\13\
Thunderstone is a fantasy deck-building game. Fight the evils of the dungeon to prove your worth. Gain powerful weaponry and level into new and mighty hero classes. Claim the best cards and survive to take the Thunderstone.

RATING: 7
Thunderstone doesn't play as smoothly as Dominion, nor are its card interactions as deep. As a matter of fact, there really isn't much in the way of combo plays at all. Most turns consist of laying down your entire hand all at once and resolving it. If this sounds awful to you, know this, it's actually not.

Despite the relatively simplistic way that cards are resolved, the experience usually provides a lot more fun than your average game of Dominion. I don't know if it's because the theme is so immersive, such as the game allowing you to level up your drafted heroes into more powerful versions after they kill stuff, or if it's simply just more fun to kill monsters than buy property...but Thunderstone feels like a more complete effort than Dominion, especially when comparing the base sets of the two games.

I have completely switched over to Richard Launius and Tom Vasel's Epic house rules, because they stretch the theme even further and make Thunderstone an even richer experience.

RATING: 8
To get the elephant in the room out of the way, if I had to pick only Dominion or this, I'd take Dominion. That said, there are things I think Thunderstone does better (diversity in abilities meaning that it sometimes makes sense to buy less powerful cards, the different options for each turn meaning that you're rarely "wasting" a turn), and I think they're different enough to justify having both. As far as Thunderstone on its own, I think it might be a little long for what it is, and I'm told that going purely random with setup will sometimes result in clunky games (which I could see), but all in all I think it provides a good gameplay experience, and while I think the "deckbuilding with a purpose" tagline is a bit tacky, it really does feel like you're building up to something rather than just building. (I don't think "just building" in Dominion is a bad thing, but I know some do.)

RATING: 8
Thunderstone is a definite improvement on Dominion:

1) Thunderstone seems slower paced, making it more forgiving in the early stages of the game and mitigating the gratuitous shuffling required by Dominion.

2) Dungeon delving to conquer monsters is a more interesting mechanic for victory points than simply purchasing land.

3) Rest enables all players to easily eliminate unwanted cards from their deck.  (Something which can be difficult and frustrating in Dominion.)

4) Thunderstone is more thematic.  I had reservations that Thunderstone's theme would work for a deck building game, but overall I think it fits the game play fairly well.

One thing that I didn't particularly like about Thunderstone was the implementation of traps and treasures.  They seemed to simply increase randomness rather than improve game play.

Thank you AEG for your generosity!

RATING: 9
Similar to Dominion, but Thunderstone blows it away in almost every aspect.  There's a ton of theme with the various monsters in the dungeon.  It's fast-paced with virtually no downtime, since everyone's turn goes quickly and you prepare for your own turn while the others are taking theirs.  But most of all, the difference is the dungeon - every turn you have a choice of battling monsters in the dungeon or adding heroes, spells, weapons, or accessories from the village.  There's randomness because of the shuffling each turn to produce your hand, but it's still up to you to create a deck that is versatile enough to work with most combinations that can come up.  There's annoying setup similar to Dominion (but mitigated if you organize the cards when you put it away), and the stats on the cards are not marked intuitively, so you just have to remember what each number or marking means.  Despite the nitpicks, still great overall.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 4
The rules as written feel like an inferior game to most modern deckbuilders, and even the mother of the genre, Dominion. Thunderstone is much longer with less bang for your buck. Sure, I love the theme and graphics of Thunderstone, as an old roleplayer it's a great fit, but the gameplay fails to live up to its promise.

The [filepage=70684][b]Epic Thunderstone[/b][/filepage] variant devised by Richard Lanius, and evangelized and modified by Tom Vasel improves the game somewhat, but there is too little XP currency in the game when not being allowed to buy level 2+ Heroes and that slows the game down further, and sucks all the fun out of it. I've tried to address this with my own variant of [filepage=70684][b]Epic Thunderstone[/b][/filepage].

I may rate Epic Thunderstone with my variants a 7, while the regular game only deserves a 4.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
[b]THE FLAMING SWORD:[/b]

1. Excellent artwork.
2. The greatest theme a geek could wish for, other than Star Wars, I suppose.
3. Great deck building mechanisms.
4. Lots of cool decisions.
5. Varying paths to victory.
6. Huge amount of variation - expansions can only improve this.
7. Training a dungeon-delving team (as a Gandalf-like figure) and then setting them loose is fun - even it's an abstract-ish way of playing D&D.
8. Rules and abilities fit the theme, and not the other way around.
9. Expandable - not collectable.

[b]THE NOXIOUS SLAG:[/b]

1. Dominion clone.
2. Crappy rulebook. Though I found it easy to explain to a couple of non-gamers.
3. Some head-scratching card rule interpretations (Dwarf Jannisay, one of the Oozes, Town guard, etc).
4. No traps or tricks in the dungeon! I eagerly await an expansion to resolve this oversight.
5. No giant spiders, either. Okay, I like my dungeon complexes to house spiders and bears. No, I won't bloody keep it down!
6. Dominion is still the "purer" design, I've decided. Maybe, probably, one Thunderstone expansion might kill off Dominion for good in my group, especially if it has spiders, traps, and bears...
7. Missing a dungeon "boss" who guards the Stone itself.
8. The Thunderstone seems like an easy design shot at  a macguffin - why not have a princess or prince who needs rescuing?
9. Less deck-churning than Dominion (at the moment). Some might see this as an advantage.


Some of the comments here really shout the game down for being an unoriginal, Dominion-clone, fantasy rip-off, stand on the shoulder of giants game.

Come on, give this game a break. I feel that knocking points off a game score for not possessing an "original" design is gross stupidity. If you don't enjoy playing Thunderstone, then say so; don't slap it down for mimicing another game. No one beats up, the frankly awful, Race for the Galaxy for cloning San Juan. Most games are descendants of other designs.

The defence rests, m'lud.

I own all the expansions. More is certainly better in the Thunderstone universe. I will 'start' to get picky after Thornwood Siege expansion box. I promise!

RATING: 6.5
I am also of the opinion that this is a better implementation of the deck building mechanic than Dominion.  Yes, in this case I do believe that theme is important and I'm not just accumulating victory points for the sake of it.  There is a sense of progression (in upgrading your heroes) and purpose (killing monster for experience and VP), so it appeals greatly to someone like me that grew up and still enjoys RPG.  I don't think it's too far fetched to claim that Thunderstone is a dungeon crawler/exploration lite.

My biggest complaint is that one's experience could be greatly dampened by a combination of bad hand and monster draw.  Thereby resulting in a lot of village rounds and not enough creature slaying.  Granted this could be argued that the person simply needs to make a better and more efficient deck, but you can't deny that luck is a huge factor regardless how fine tuned your deck is.

Anyway, I look forward to the addition of different mechanics, especially other ways to obtain VP and maybe even ones that will given penalty like the curse cards in Dominion.

RATING: 7.8
First thing that comes to my mind when I read the line deck-building game, was “it’s a Dominion-clone.” And at it’s base, it is a Dominion clone. But there is more in this one, then there is in Dominion.
Dominion is very easy to explain to new players, as there are always the same steps in a players turn:

    Draw 5 cards
    You may play an action (or more if a cards allows you)
    Purchase a card (or more if a cards allows you)
    Discard your cards.

And that’s all there is in Dominion. Nothing more. Very easy, every turn the same, and still we both like it a lot. Would Thunderstone be as nice or nicer, or would it just be another clone of a succesfull game? First step was to sort the huge amount of cards that were in the box. And that was a pretty hard job to do, as we got 4 cards of a kind, then 3 of another, then 1 of the first kind, then a couple of cards of the third kind, but we managed to sort them out, and the result was a table full of small stacks of cards. Placed everything in the box (of which I have to say, I like the solution Dominion gives more. The dividers delivered with the game, are just too small to look up the cards easy.), and started to set up the first game. We used the cards that were recommended in the rulesbook (ver 1.4). And started the game after reading the rules and explaing them to M..

It took us almost 2 hours to play our first game. We had several things to look up (what does a card do/mean?), but we both enjoyed it very much. My conclusion is that I think that it is a better game then Dominion is. M. is not sure about that. Mainly because of the difficulties she has with the English text on the cards. It’s harder for her to understand it, then it’s for me. Most of the cards were pretty clear to me, so I could explain them to M.. Why do I think it’s a better game then Dominion is? Well, that’s pretty easy to explain. I think it’s better then Dominion, just because of one word. And that word is or. That same word makes the game harder to explain to people, because those two letters give you such a lot of possibilities. Let me explain.

A players turn starts and ends the same way a turn in Dominion starts and ends.  Draw cards and discard your cards. And then comes the word or in the game.

    You can make a purschase or
    You can enter the dungeon or
    You rest

If you decide for the first option, then it’s just like Dominion. You may play an action and purchase a card (additionaly, you can upgrade a hero).
If you decide for the second option, you count your attack value, and you try to fight a monster (after resolving the monster cards).
If you decide for option three, you destroy a card (which can be handy, because you can get rid of the cards you don’t like anymore).

While in Domion, you just buy victory points, in Thunderstone you have to decide what to do. Go for VP’s, or make you deck stronger by purchusing or destroying cards. Sometimes it’s a really tough decision you have to make. You have the money needed for the one card you really want to have, but you can also fight a monster and get the VP’s, while in your next turn it might be possible that you could do neither of them. These, sometimes difficult, decissions makes it a better game for me then Dominion is. I’m sure the same will count for M., when she understands all of the cards. That Thunderstone is a harder game then Dominion, becomes already clear by just looking at the playing time. 60 minutes for Thunderstone agaist 30 minutes for Dominion. I just have to decide what to do for the sollution with the dividers. Buy the expansion in which they are in, or make them myself. If it’s up to me, it’s going to be the first sollution.

RATING: 8
Thunderstone comes off as a dungeon-crawl Dominion. The mechanics are very similar, but Thunderstone has far more immersive gameplay. It is more fun to play for the experience.

The problem with this game is that it is significantly less streamlined than Dominion. There are a lot of cards flying around, and most of them get in the way at least half of the time. For rookie players it usually means ending up with an awful deck while the others march through the dungeon.
